2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`

4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Node.js child_process Command Injection Guards

## Your Task

Find all JavaScript and C++ source files in nodejs/node that implement input validation and command injection prevention for the child_process module. Identify: the normalizeSpawnArguments function with null-byte validation, the exec/execFile/spawn entry points, the internal ChildProcess class that interfaces with C++, the ProcessWrap native binding, and the validator functions (validateArgumentNullCheck) used to prevent injection.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/node--v22.13.0.

I am thinking...: Now I have a comprehensive picture of all the relevant files. Let me summarize what I've found:

1. **`lib/child_process.js`** - The main public API file containing:
   - `exec()` - entry point for shell command execution
   - `execFile()` - entry point for file execution
   - `spawn()` - entry point for process spawning
   - `spawnSync()` - synchronous spawn
   - `execSync()` - synchronous exec
   - `execFileSync()` - synchronous execFile
   - `fork()` - fork a new Node.js process
   - `normalizeSpawnArguments()` - normalizes and validates spawn arguments, including null-byte checks
   - `normalizeExecArgs()` - normalizes exec arguments
   - `normalizeExecFileArgs()` - normalizes execFile arguments
   - `validateArgumentNullCheck()` - validates a single argument for null bytes
   - `validateArgumentsNullCheck()` - validates an array of arguments for null bytes
   - `validateTimeout()` - validates timeout option
   - `validateMaxBuffer()` - validates maxBuffer option
   - `sanitizeKillSignal()` - sanitizes kill signal

2. **`lib/internal/child_process.js`** - Internal implementation containing:
   - `ChildProcess` class - the internal class that interfaces with C++ via `this._handle = new Process()`
   - `ChildProcess.prototype.spawn()` - the actual spawn method that calls `this._handle.spawn(options)`
   - Uses `internalBinding('process_wrap')` to get the `Process` constructor

3. **`src/process_wrap.cc`** - C++ native binding containing:
   - `ProcessWrap` class - the native binding that wraps `uv_process_t`
   - `ProcessWrap::Spawn()` - the C++ spawn method that calls `uv_spawn()`
   - `ProcessWrap::Kill()` - the C++ kill method
   - `IsWindowsBatchFile()` check to prevent spawning batch files directly on Windows

The answer has been written to `/workspace/answer.json`. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Findings Summary

### JavaScript Files

1. **`lib/child_process.js`** — The main public API with all entry points:
   - `exec()`, `execFile()`, `spawn()`, `spawnSync()`, `execSync()`, `execFileSync()`, `fork()`
   - `normalizeSpawnArguments()` — validates file, args, argv0, shell, and env key/values for null bytes
   - `normalizeExecArgs()` — validates the command string for null bytes
   - `normalizeExecFileArgs()` — validates argv0 for null bytes
   - `validateArgumentNullCheck()` — core guard: throws `ERR_INVALID_ARG_VALUE` if string contains `\u0000`
   - `validateArgumentsNullCheck()` — iterates an array calling `validateArgumentNullCheck` on each element

2. **`lib/internal/child_process.js`** — Internal implementation:
   - `ChildProcess` class — extends EventEmitter, holds `this._handle = new Process()` (the C++ binding)
   - `ChildProcess.prototype.spawn()` — bridges JS to C++ via `this._handle.spawn(options)`

3. **`lib/internal/child_process/serialization.js`** — IPC message serialization

### C++ Files

4. **`src/process_wrap.cc`** — Native binding for async spawning:
   - `ProcessWrap` class — wraps `uv_process_t`, exposes `spawn` and `kill` methods
   - `ProcessWrap::Spawn()` — checks permissions, rejects Windows batch files, calls `uv_spawn()`

5. **`src/spawn_sync.cc`** — Native binding for synchronous spawning:
   - `SyncProcessRunner::ParseOptions()` — also rejects Windows batch files

6. **`src/util-inl.h`** — `IsWindowsBatchFile()` implementation (regex-based `.bat`/`.cmd` detection)

7. **`src/util.h`** — `IsWindowsBatchFile()` declaration

### Test File

8. **`test/parallel/test-child-process-reject-null-bytes.js`** — Regression test for null-byte injecti

The task is complete. The `/workspace/answer.json` file has been created with comprehensive findings. Here's a concise summary of what was identified:

## Task Complete

The answer file at `/workspace/answer.json` documents all relevant files and symbols for Node.js child_process command injection guards:

### Key Files Found

| File | Role |
|------|------|
| `lib/child_process.js` | Public API entry points + all validation/guard functions |
| `lib/internal/child_process.js` | Internal `ChildProcess` class bridging JS↔C++ |
| `src/process_wrap.cc` | C++ `ProcessWrap` native binding (async spawn) |
| `src/spawn_sync.cc` | C++ `SyncProcessRunner` (sync spawn) |
| `src/util-inl.h` | `IsWindowsBatchFile()` implementation |
| `src/util.h` | `IsWindowsBatchFile()` declaration |
| `lib/internal/child_process/serialization.js` | IPC serialization |
| `test/parallel/test-child-process-reject-null-bytes.js` | Null-byte regression tests |

### Security Chain
1. **`exec`/`execFile`/`spawn`/`fork`** (lib/child_process.js) → call normalization functions
2. **`normalizeSpawnArguments`/`normalizeExecArgs`** → call **`validateArgumentNullCheck`** to reject `\0` bytes in file, args, env, shell, argv0, cwd, execPath, execArgv
3. **`spawn()`** → creates `new ChildProcess()` → calls `child.spawn(options)`
4. **`ChildProcess.prototype.spawn`** (lib/internal/child_process.js) → calls `this._handle.spawn(options)` (C++ bridge)
5. **`ProcessWrap::Spawn`** (src/process_wrap.cc) → checks permissions + rejects Windows `.bat`/`.cmd` via `IsWindowsBatchFile()` → calls `uv_spawn()`
